  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_56a879b4-1813-4a20-a1bc-67e004a3af90'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer68526422848657756">Now available in paperback, The Fire Thief hilariously reimagines the myth of Prometheus, the Greek demigod who stole fire from the gods and gave it to the human race. To escape the gods' revenge, Prometheus travels through time to Eden City in 1858. There, he befriends a young orphan, actor, and petty criminal named Jim. When Jim runs into trouble with the law, Prometheus</span>
  <span id="freeText68526422848657756" style="display:none">Now available in paperback, The Fire Thief hilariously reimagines the myth of Prometheus, the Greek demigod who stole fire from the gods and gave it to the human race. To escape the gods' revenge, Prometheus travels through time to Eden City in 1858. There, he befriends a young orphan, actor, and petty criminal named Jim. When Jim runs into trouble with the law, Prometheus is torn -- if he uses his powers to get his friend out of trouble, he will betray his hiding place to the gods. Terry Deary masterfully interweaves two plots, with action jumping at a whirlwind pace from Mount Olympus to the seedy taverns and elegant mansions of Victorian Eden City. Packed with puns, wisecracks, and sarcastic footnotes, The Fire Thief turns Greek mythology into a laughing matter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="68526422848657756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12617414514718689282">The Fire Thief (Fire Thief Trilogy #1), Terry Deary <br/><br/>The story tells of Prometheus when he is chained to a rock and about to have his liver ripped out by the Fury, but instead he is freed by the hero Hercules. <br/><br/>He grabs the Fury, breaks its neck and runs away after he has been freed from the mountain he was chained to, by his cousin Zeus, the Greek god of lightning and ruler of the sky. Zeus sends him on a quest to find a true human hero. <br/><br/>He gives Prometheus a ring because he promised that Prometh</span>
  <span id="freeText12617414514718689282" style="display:none">The Fire Thief (Fire Thief Trilogy #1), Terry Deary <br /><br />The story tells of Prometheus when he is chained to a rock and about to have his liver ripped out by the Fury, but instead he is freed by the hero Hercules. <br /><br />He grabs the Fury, breaks its neck and runs away after he has been freed from the mountain he was chained to, by his cousin Zeus, the Greek god of lightning and ruler of the sky. Zeus sends him on a quest to find a true human hero. <br /><br />He gives Prometheus a ring because he promised that Prometheus will always be chained to that rock. This means that Zeus can always find him as well. Prometheus travels into the future with a pair of magical wings. <br /><br />He lands in Eden City and is helped by Uncle Edward and young Jim, a pair of robbers. The Fury is bent on revenge and Theus must complete this task while avoiding the Fury, who is supposed to eat his liver everyday for eternity. <br /><br />There, Jim and Uncle Edward stay at Storm Inn where they meet January Storm. They came to Eden City to steal riches from the Mucklethrift Manor. They usually put a play on and while they are doing it, Jim goes and steals the riches. <br /><br />When Prometheus came, he was strong so he could help the robbers carry the coffin which they put the stolen goods in. They are successful but Mayor Walter Tweed catches them and demands to get 1/3 of the stolen riches. The Mayor makes a fake deal with the Uncle Edward pretending that the police would not catch the robbers, Uncle Edward and Jim.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز چهاردهم ماه جولای سال 2009 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: آتش دزد کتاب اول از سه گانه آتش دزد؛ نویسنده: تری دیری؛ مترجم: حسین ابراهیمی (الوند)؛ تهران، افق، 1388، در 290ص؛ شابک 9789643693916؛ چاپ دوم 1388؛ چاپ سوم 1389؛ چاپ هفتم 1391؛ موضوع داستانها اساطیری یونانی برای کودکان از نویسندگان انگلیسی سده 21م<br /><br />برداشت تازه ای از داستان پرومتئوس ایزد یونانی که جرمش دزدیدن آنش بود، و زئوس برای مجازاتش پرنده ای غول آسا را مامور کرد، هر روز جگرش بیرون بکشد، هرکول او را نجات داد، کتاب برای نوجوانان است؛<br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1830556989" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830556989" />
    <a title=" Li&#39;l Owl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48372551-li-l-owl"><img alt=" Li&#39;l Owl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605862749p2/48372551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830556989?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Li&#39;l Owl" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Li&#39;l Owl" href="/user/show/48372551-li-l-owl"> Li&#39;l Owl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=fantasy-magic-adventure">fantasy-magic-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=owl-s-books-own">owl-s-books-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=mythology-folklore-legend">mythology-folklore-legend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830556989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10949906335429593142">From the back cover of the book:<br/><br/>Here are the Greek gods like you've never seen them before! <br/>In this hilarious, time traveling tale, acclaimed author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10038.Terry_Deary' title='Terry Deary' rel='nofollow noopener'>Terry Deary</a> reinvents the Greek myth of Prometheus, who stole fire from the gods. On the run from Zeus's avenging eagle, Prometheus hides out in Victorian Eden City, where he befriends an orphan named Jim. Packed with puns, wisecracking gods, and sarcastic footnotes, the fire Thief is a rollicking blend of action, anarchy, and narrative tradition. <br/><br/><i>'</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10949906335429593142" style="display:none">From the back cover of the book:<br /><br />Here are the Greek gods like you've never seen them before! <br />In this hilarious, time traveling tale, acclaimed author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10038.Terry_Deary" title="Terry Deary" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Deary</a> reinvents the Greek myth of Prometheus, who stole fire from the gods. On the run from Zeus's avenging eagle, Prometheus hides out in Victorian Eden City, where he befriends an orphan named Jim. Packed with puns, wisecracking gods, and sarcastic footnotes, the fire Thief is a rollicking blend of action, anarchy, and narrative tradition. <br /><br /><i>' at last, the two halves of our story come together. "And it's about time! " that ugly reader with a face like a potato says. Well, let me tell you, potato face, everything comes to him who waits --or her who waits...or it that waits. Whatever. If you haven't guessed who walked through those swinging doors you haven't been paying attention.<br /><br />The Chimera had three heads -- lion, goat, and snake.³³ its body was also mixed, having the front part of a lion, the middle of a goat, and the tail of a snake. It wasn't pretty, and it wasn't the sort of monster that you'd want to meet in an alley at night. To be honest, you wouldn't want to meet it in the day time either.<br /><br />³³ Being born with three heads is no fun, do not mock the Chimera. When one of those heads is a goat head, then it is a real nightmare. I mean, have you ever smelled a goat's breath? Imagine being stuck next to that for all of your life. No wonder the Chimera was bad-tempered. By the way... Do NOT try smelling of goats breath to check what I say. If you die as a result, you will NOT be given your money back for this book.</i><br /><br />I decided to read something a little different than my usual genre of mystery, suspense, thriller, crime. <br />I've had this book in my library for what seems like forever. I don't know why I've never read it until now but I'm so glad I finally did! This is book one of <i>The Fire Thief Trilogy.</i> The second is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1678247.Flight_of_the_Fire_Thief__Fire_Thief_Trilogy___2_" title="Flight of the Fire Thief (Fire Thief Trilogy, #2) by Terry Deary" rel="nofollow noopener">Flight of the Fire Thief</a> which I will be reading in the very near future! This is a delightful, laugh a minute read! It is craftily written, as well, so much so that I had to see what would happen next! I read it in one sitting! What a treat! I simply loved it! I highly recommend it!! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10949906335429593142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_85703334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85703334" />
    <a title="Cody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2698198-cody"><img alt="Cody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257746547p2/2698198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85703334?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody" href="/user/show/2698198-cody">Cody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Other Format 9781442032019" href="/book/show/7052348-the-fire-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85703334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5822482529718918920">Fire Thief<br/><br/>	On a scale of 1 to 10 I would rate this book at no more than a 6. Although it is entertaining it lacks intellect and depth. Any subtleties this book has a spoon-fed to the reader through direct narration or with the oh too convenient author’s sub analysis of the book as you are reading it. Terry Deary very clearly wrote this book for children in the 5th or 6th grade level as it lacks any kind of rhetorical skill or literary merit. <br/>	I would caution anyone that expects to get something </span>
  <span id="freeText5822482529718918920" style="display:none">Fire Thief<br /><br />	On a scale of 1 to 10 I would rate this book at no more than a 6. Although it is entertaining it lacks intellect and depth. Any subtleties this book has a spoon-fed to the reader through direct narration or with the oh too convenient author’s sub analysis of the book as you are reading it. Terry Deary very clearly wrote this book for children in the 5th or 6th grade level as it lacks any kind of rhetorical skill or literary merit. <br />	I would caution anyone that expects to get something out of reading this book but for a casual days read, (and it takes no more than a solid day to read this entire novel) it is entertaining. On a positive note I thought it was quite interesting that the author was able to combine both Greek mythology and the 19th century in a direct manor, now that doesn’t mean to say its as difficult as writing in the 2nd person but it quite a challenge as both time periods have literally nothing in common other than the mere existence of humans. <br />	The development of characters isn’t really present; they are established in the first couple chapters and not expanded on in any kind of depth or analysis. Not one character is faced with any kind of moral choice or incidence where he or she must make a choice that determines their nature. Even the climax of the story is just a turning point that any reader could have predicted after chapter 10 or 11. <br />	As far as messages go the whole book ended up being a subtle pitch on global warming, and how we need to start preserving the planet now before it’s too late. Big disappointment Mr. Deary, because as much as you might care about the planet and believe the scam that global warming is, this book really has no place for that kind of sentiment. One message that this book does offer is no matter how evil or corrupt someone is they can still show compassion and should still be forgiven; which speaks strongly to kids (for whom this book is clearly intended) but what about the fact that Jim and Uncle Edward are thieves? And have been their whole lives? Should not they be punished for their wicked ways? A moment of kindness and repentance can’t possibly redeem a person of a lifetime of treachery and deceit. <br />	One particular thing that bothered me was the lack of research on behalf of the author. Not everyone knows, but anyone with internet access can easily discover is that when someone is hanged it is not suffocation that kills them, it is in fact the breaking of their neck by the large knot in the rope. If this little indiscretion had been taken care of at the source then approximately 20-30 pages would simply disappear. There were a few other minor issues I had, one being the uneducated nature of Prometheus, how could a God be so stupid? If someone had the ability to time travel I think that they would explore the possibilities a bit more and therefore at bare minimum know about the social graces of that time period. And another thing, the Greeks had schools for their young and adolescents, the book implies that the Greek society produced from birth completely literate and capable children, which is of course ridiculous. <br />	Overall, and despite my negative nature to find fault in this book it was a enjoyable read. If you are interested in Greek mythology then you might want to read this book, just not for any kind of education on mythology itself.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5822482529718918920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer185390426" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1419966323268441779">This was a little disappointing. The story itself was fine--the angle on the Prometheus myth was interesting. But the narrative style was incredibly distracting. The narrator, in addition to an aside to the reader at the beginning of each chapter, peppers the narrative with footnoted asides to the reader as well. I would have been completely happy reading the story without those blasted asides. I hate it when the narrator tries to converse with the reader. A stylistic thing, to be sure, but defi</span>
  <span id="freeText1419966323268441779" style="display:none">This was a little disappointing. The story itself was fine--the angle on the Prometheus myth was interesting. But the narrative style was incredibly distracting. The narrator, in addition to an aside to the reader at the beginning of each chapter, peppers the narrative with footnoted asides to the reader as well. I would have been completely happy reading the story without those blasted asides. I hate it when the narrator tries to converse with the reader. A stylistic thing, to be sure, but definitely something that irritates me enough that I'm not sure I'd bother looking for book two in the series...</span>

<div id="review_938108574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/938108574" />
    <a title="Tavian Sim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26602868-tavian-sim"><img alt="Tavian Sim" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/938108574?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tavian Sim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tavian Sim" href="/user/show/26602868-tavian-sim">Tavian Sim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938108574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10597615353749941104">The book The Fire Thief in my opinion, is a okay written book. The story and plot itself is great though. The book becomes kind of confusing when he changes from one position to another really frequently during the book. I love the Greek Gods and anything that has to do with them so that kept me entertained enough to keep reading. The book is very boring at points though. I wasn't a fan of the setting in the 1700's , its just boring to me. But when the Gods are conversing and in their setting th</span>
  <span id="freeText10597615353749941104" style="display:none">The book The Fire Thief in my opinion, is a okay written book. The story and plot itself is great though. The book becomes kind of confusing when he changes from one position to another really frequently during the book. I love the Greek Gods and anything that has to do with them so that kept me entertained enough to keep reading. The book is very boring at points though. I wasn't a fan of the setting in the 1700's , its just boring to me. But when the Gods are conversing and in their setting the story was quite interesting. The main idea of the story is good too, about Prometheus trying to find a worthy human hero that will prove to Zeus that they deserve fire. I wasn't too happy about the fact that they made Prometheus out to be an idiot though. The author also makes it more entertaining throughout the book by placing footnotes at the bottom of every other page or so that are usually very sarcastic and humorous. It is honestly a very easy read probably made for the boys of a younger age probably around 12. It's a quick read but honestly I wouldn't recommend it. A lot of people wouldn't enjoy it and I barely did so, but if you are into Greek mythology and sarcasm by the author, I think you might have a chance of enjoying this book. I also feel as if its a knockoff of the book "The Lightning Thief" but that's just me, and eh its nowhere as good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10597615353749941104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297821687" />
    <a title="Clara Publius" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8010401-clara-publius"><img alt="Clara Publius" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297821687?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clara Publius" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clara Publius" href="/user/show/8010401-clara-publius">Clara Publius</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297821687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9831965534277314330">In the Fire Thief, Prometheus had made a deal with Zeus. He would have a limited amount of time to find a worthy human hero to prove to Zeus that humans deserved the gift of fire. Then he meets a pair of thieves when he travels into the future to 1858. He ends up helping them with their theft. I enjoyed the book but it wasn’t my favorite. Normally, Prometheus is described as cunning and crafty but in this book, he is clueless, humble and generous. It also contains a lot of mythology and Greek Go</span>
  <span id="freeText9831965534277314330" style="display:none">In the Fire Thief, Prometheus had made a deal with Zeus. He would have a limited amount of time to find a worthy human hero to prove to Zeus that humans deserved the gift of fire. Then he meets a pair of thieves when he travels into the future to 1858. He ends up helping them with their theft. I enjoyed the book but it wasn’t my favorite. Normally, Prometheus is described as cunning and crafty but in this book, he is clueless, humble and generous. It also contains a lot of mythology and Greek Gods. The personalities of the characters are well developed. The little, orphaned boy, Jim is jumpy. shy and timid while the other thief, Uncle Eddie, is sarcastic. The plot is, however, really simple and has an abrupt ending. The old-fashioned setting is also very hard to connect to. The Lightening Thief series is a better alternative if you want a good story with mythology.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9831965534277314330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimia" href="/user/show/71412015-kimia">Kimia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17556910801961915783">. (نقد فارسى در پايين)<br/>Good, but damaged by the style!! I liked the plot of the story. Such a great idea to adapt from the myth of the Greek Titan, Prometheus. The moral ideas in the story were remarkable (except for the kids name-calling and bullying each other, and the bold gender roles). But what I hated was the very very so much direct descriptions and the self-spoiling that the writer clearly did on purpose and thought would be funny. It’s like having an annoying friend tutoring you on a mov</span>
  <span id="freeText17556910801961915783" style="display:none">. (نقد فارسى در پايين)<br />Good, but damaged by the style!! I liked the plot of the story. Such a great idea to adapt from the myth of the Greek Titan, Prometheus. The moral ideas in the story were remarkable (except for the kids name-calling and bullying each other, and the bold gender roles). But what I hated was the very very so much direct descriptions and the self-spoiling that the writer clearly did on purpose and thought would be funny. It’s like having an annoying friend tutoring you on a movie you’re already watching. I think the writer wanted to give writing lessons to kids alongside, but it kinda turned out bad. Things like “You see the plot twist I made here?? I’m sure you’re surprised” (yes, Terry, we saw the plot twist and we liked it UNTIL YOU POINTED IT OUT!!), or “I bet you’re asking yourself what was I doing there?! But in order to find that out, you have to resume. Now, stop nagging and get back to the story!!” (What did you possibly think we were gonna do, Terry?? 🙄)<br /><br />خوب بود ولى نويسنده گند زد بهش. 😅 پلات داستان رو دوست داشتم. ارائه كردن فرم جديدى از اساطير يونان باستان رو كار خلاقانه اى ميدونم. درونمايه داستان عالى بود. تنها چيزى كه دوست نداشتم اون زيرنويس هاى عمدى نويسنده بود كه فكر ميكرد خيلى بامزه ست. :| به نظرم قشنگتره بذاريم خواننده خودش نتيجه بگيره. ولى نويسنده اينقدر همه چيزو بسيار بسيار بسيار مستقيم توصيف كرده و بيش از اندازه توضيح داده و به جوك هاى خودش خنديده و از خودش تعريف كرده كه لوس شده!! عين يه دوست اعصاب خورد كن كه وقتى دارى فيلم ميبينى نكات بسيار بديهى فيلم رو برات توضيح ميده :))) مثلاً "حتماً الان داريد با خودتان ميگوييد كه من آنجا چه كار ميكردم؟ براى اينكه بفهميد، بايد داستان را ادامه دهيد. خب ديگر، كمتر غر بزنيد و به ادامه داستان بازگرديد!" خب بزرگوار، نميگفتى هم داشتيم همين كارو ميكرديم ديگه!! :| يا مثلاً يه چيز جالب تو كتاب ميبينى و توى دلت ميگى: "واى چه توصيف جالبى! چه قدر خوب با كلمات بازى كرده" و درست همين لحظه ميبينى تو پاورقى نوشته: "بله دوستان ديديد چيكار كردم؟! من همچين نويسنده اى هستم!!" كاملاً مشخصه كه داره سعى ميكنه در كنار داستان پردازى به بچه ها آموزش نويسندگى هم بده، ولى كاش اين كارو نمى كرد. يه مسئله ديگه اينكه ترجيح ميدادم رفتارهايى در بچه ها مثل مسخره كردن قيافه و دادن القابى مثل "زشت" به همديگه، يا كليشه هاى پررنگ جنسيتى رو در كتاب هاى گروه سنى كودك و نوجوان نبينم.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17556910801961915783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_775515528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/775515528" />
    <a title="Erika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4532400-erika"><img alt="Erika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523323123p2/4532400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/775515528?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erika" href="/user/show/4532400-erika">Erika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330521635" href="/book/show/10443330-the-fire-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4532400-erika?shelf=children-literature">children-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer775515528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16241818788030525105">I feel so harsh giving such a low rating to a book for kiddies, but then I realized I have read and loved other books on this category. The problem laid on this book. The premise was interesting. that's why I got the thing on the first place. I'm up for anything related to Greek mythology. But as much as I wanted to like the story it just did not work for me. Everything was so inconsistent. Things starts all epic (a chained god in suffering, his release and retaliation) but then it all goes wron</span>
  <span id="freeText16241818788030525105" style="display:none">I feel so harsh giving such a low rating to a book for kiddies, but then I realized I have read and loved other books on this category. The problem laid on this book. The premise was interesting. that's why I got the thing on the first place. I'm up for anything related to Greek mythology. But as much as I wanted to like the story it just did not work for me. Everything was so inconsistent. Things starts all epic (a chained god in suffering, his release and retaliation) but then it all goes wrong and he's a silly doofus. Every single deity, no, scratch that, every single <i> character</i> is portrayed as dumb. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I mean, what the hell with Zeus? He wants to punish Prometheus, then he lets him go, then he tries to destroy the humans, then he wants to save Prometheus <i> and</i> the humans. It was all so confusing, there was no lead up to his random changes of heart. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It was so unrealistic that it started to piss me off. Everything had to be turned into a goofy affair. Reading this was like watching the most mindless, silly cartoon. And, oh, the unbearable, never-ending, <i>unnecessary</i> footnotes! "Guess what's gonna happen now, reader? Sure you can't! Because, you know, blah blah blah." I read up to four of those and gave them up entirely. Same thing with the recaps at the beginning of each chapter. I mean, come on. I freaking remember what happened ten pages ago! Gave them up as well after the first three chapters. Maybe the author had to find a way to make the book a few pages longer and came up with this brilliant plan.<br /><br />I don't like this book as an adult and I wouldn't have liked it as a kid. Feels too dumbed down and silly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16241818788030525105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_446760434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/446760434" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10669041-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341356072p2/10669041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/446760434?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/10669041-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer446760434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer299922390222630706">I think this book would be attractive to any students in KYS2. It is a humorous time travelling book that re-invents the Greek myths of Prometheus combined with the daily struggle of life that occurred in the Victorian era. In this story Prometheus has stolen fire from the Gods and has given this great gift to the humans on earth. Zeus angry at this action sends his avenging eagle named the Fury to punish him eternally by prodding at his internal organs on a daily basis. This leads to Prometheus</span>
  <span id="freeText299922390222630706" style="display:none">I think this book would be attractive to any students in KYS2. It is a humorous time travelling book that re-invents the Greek myths of Prometheus combined with the daily struggle of life that occurred in the Victorian era. In this story Prometheus has stolen fire from the Gods and has given this great gift to the humans on earth. Zeus angry at this action sends his avenging eagle named the Fury to punish him eternally by prodding at his internal organs on a daily basis. This leads to Prometheus fleeing to earth and hiding out in a dreary smog covered city called Eden which is currently experiencing a depression. Prometheus completely ignorant of Victorian ways quickly befriends a cheeky orphan named Jim and his trickster phony Uncle Edward. The trio embark on nail biting criminal activities with Prometheus none the wiser. He is led to believe that the pair are in the acting business and together they travel to rich and grand houses to put on wonderful and elaborate shows. <br />This story is packed with clever puns, sarcastic footnotes and an interesting insight into two very different eras one fictional and the other mythological. This book weaves the two together in a funny and cheeky way. This would be good for independent reading or as a starter to creative writing. The author cleverly uses footnotes to introduce how he is creating the story so the reader feels more in touch with the author. The footnotes use lots of humour to get his techniques across. I think this book gives a good insight into how to create an interesting and captivating story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="299922390222630706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3235003931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16996753781125917425">The Greek Mythology Novel, “The Fire Thief” by Terry Deary tells a story about how the Greek Titan, Prometheus, stole fire from the gods and gave them to humans. Once Prometheus stole fire from the gods and gave it to the humans, he was chained to a rock for 200 years as a punishment by his cousin Zeus, getting his liver torn out by a fury for 100 years. Prometheus was given a task to go find a true human hero by Zeus the lightning god that rules the sky in Greek Mythology. Prometheus meets and </span>
  <span id="freeText16996753781125917425" style="display:none">The Greek Mythology Novel, “The Fire Thief” by Terry Deary tells a story about how the Greek Titan, Prometheus, stole fire from the gods and gave them to humans. Once Prometheus stole fire from the gods and gave it to the humans, he was chained to a rock for 200 years as a punishment by his cousin Zeus, getting his liver torn out by a fury for 100 years. Prometheus was given a task to go find a true human hero by Zeus the lightning god that rules the sky in Greek Mythology. Prometheus meets and helps a two man group of robbers by the name’s of Jim and Edward, they rob the Mucklethrift Manor. They robbed the Manor but then was caught by the mayor and the mayor lied saying that they wouldn’t get caught by the police if they shared one-third of the stolen goods. All in all, Prometheus stole and gave fire to the humans, then was given a task to find a true human hero, then met a pair of robbers and helped them rob Mucklethrift Manor, finally they robbed the manor but were caught and lied to. I would rate this book a 3 out of 5 stars because the author wrote small notes at the start of every chapter. But I didn't like how the author switched stories at the start of the book. I would recommend this book to others who like Greek Mythology.</span>

I like how it included many elements, not just the story about Prometheus stealing fire from the gods and giving it to the humans. I also like how instead of making the book in the perspective of Prometheus, it was in the perspective of the orphan Jim. I read the book very quickly, and it wasn't all that long.   <span id="freeText3112755012979621461" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book and its take on Greek mythology. I like how it included many elements, not just the story about Prometheus stealing fire from the gods and giving it to the humans. I also like how instead of making the book in the perspective of Prometheus, it was in the perspective of the orphan Jim. I read the book very quickly, and it wasn't all that long. There were quite a few interesting twists, and the one that stands out to me was not explained until afterwards (the footnotes say that it is because the chapters got all mixed up/in the wrong order). I also like how the book has a bit of time travelling element in it, and it neither takes place in modern day, or entirely in ancient Greece (only parts of it are in ancient Greece.)</span>

<div id="review_2966244503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2966244503" />
    <a title="Travis H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61546533-travis-h"><img alt="Travis H" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2966244503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3304209873240688315">This story is about mythology, specifically Prometheus stealing fire from the gods and finding a human hero to kill the raven that ate out his liver every day while chained to a cliff face by Zeus. Taking place at the very beginning of humanity, Deary does a great job of putting his own twist on a classic story using humor and creativity in his writing. With two different story lines seamlessly combining into one, Deary's The Fire Thief is truly a steal.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_1251641'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1251641._"><img alt="هری پاتر و محفل ققنوس - کتاب پنجم جلد یک از سه" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1361550578l/1251641._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MhVWppw5WWSZnSN4xI7cO4SbFzWXfIAhAEjIMpSkTPD8K2CQF4/H1g0pdST0RbO4+KxU64wsuXmft1w+wBULxg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13949973862087168592">A former actor, theatre-director and drama teacher, Deary says he began writing when he was 29. Most famously, he is one of the authors of the Horrible Histories series of books popular among children for their disgusting details, gory information and humorous pictures and among adults for getting children interested in history. Books in the series have been widely translated into other languages </span>
  <span id="freeText13949973862087168592" style="display:none">A former actor, theatre-director and drama teacher, Deary says he began writing when he was 29. Most famously, he is one of the authors of the Horrible Histories series of books popular among children for their disgusting details, gory information and humorous pictures and among adults for getting children interested in history. Books in the series have been widely translated into other languages and imitated.<br /><br />A cartoon series has been made of the series of books and was shown on CiTV for a period in 2002.<br /><br />The first series of a live-action comedy sketch show of the same name was shown on CBBC in 2009 and a second series is due.<br /><br />Terry is also known widely throughout children and adult reading groups alike for his True Stories series (see below for series list).<br /><br />He received an Honorary Doctorate of Education from the University of Sunderland in 2000. His numerous accolades also include the Blue Peter "Best Nonfiction Author of the Century" Award in the U.K. <br /><br />-Wikipedia</span>
